To guarantee completeness regardless of thread size, each location **fetches the full thread on demand** (`GET /rest/api/2/issue/{key}/comment`) via a new shared `useIssueComments` hook and renders it through a new shared `CommentThread` / connected `IssueComments` component (extracted from `IssueDetailPanel`), with consistent empty/loading/error states. Separately, text boxes, inputs, and the comment window now use a **subtle gradient/elevation** (new `--field-elevation-*` and `--comment-window-bg` design tokens) so field boundaries read clearly **without heavy borders in both light and dark themes**, degrading to a solid field + strong border under `prefers-contrast: more`. Text keeps **WCAG 2.1 AA** contrast in both themes (measured ≥5:1 for body text on treated fields). Presentation-only: no change to comment posting or any Jira write behavior. Full client suite GREEN (2645); production build clean.
- **SharePoint relay connect moved into the Connection Bar (feature 008)**: The SharePoint intake relay now connects from the app's unified **Connection Bar** (a new SharePoint indicator + inline panel with the draggable bookmarklet and status), like every other service — instead of the connect UI living inside the Jira Intake view. The intake pull panel is slimmed to **connection status + Pull** and points users to the Connection Bar when disconnected. Relay status is now tracked **per system** in the connection store, so ServiceNow and SharePoint statuses are independent (the legacy single relay field stays the ServiceNow mirror — no SNow regression). The app polls both relays on the same cadence. Pull/dedup/create (features 006/007) are unchanged.

### Added
- **Teams → Jira intake — one-click pull from SharePoint via browser relay (feature 007, Phase 2B)**: A new **Pull from SharePoint** panel lets a Toolbox user read the `Jira-Intake` **SharePoint List** directly through the **same browser-relay pattern** already used for ServiceNow/Jira (a bookmarklet on an authenticated SharePoint tab), instead of exporting and drag-dropping a file. Pulled List items are mapped to the existing submission shape and flow through the **unchanged** queue → dedup (feature 006) → create pipeline. The reader **resolves the List's internal column names automatically** (via the list `/fields` endpoint), including the reserved-`id` GUID column, so the user only deals with display names; it **pages through the whole List**. One-click (or optional auto-refresh while the relay tab stays connected) — no app registration, no premium connector, no stored SharePoint credentials, no inbound endpoint. Any disconnect/permission/read error creates nothing and shows a clear message; **drag-and-drop remains as a fallback**. New `sharepoint` relay system, SharePoint bookmarklet, `sharepointIntakeApi`, `mapSharePointItem`, `useSharePointPull`, and `SharePointPullPanel`; intake settings gain the SharePoint site URL + list name.
- **Teams → Jira intake — duplicate-proof creation via Jira label stamp (feature 006, Phase 2A)**: Every issue Toolbox creates from a submission is now **stamped with a Jira label `intake-<id>`** (the submission GUID), and before creating anything Toolbox **asks Jira** (label JQL search) whether a stamped issue already exists — if so it reconciles the row to that existing key and creates nothing. Jira itself becomes the source of truth for "already created," so **duplicates are impossible even across machines, re-imports, or a reset local ledger**; the local ledger stays as a fast cache. A batched pre-scan runs on import (single query for all not-locally-known rows) and a per-row guard runs at the moment of creation, covering auto-create, the bulk "Create N", per-row Create, and Retry. If the Jira check can't complete, Toolbox creates nothing and flags the row for retry (never a blind create). New `intakeLabel` + `reconcileExisting` helpers and a `searchIssuesByLabels` Jira wrapper.

### Added
- **Teams → Jira intake importer (feature 005, Phase 2)**: A new **Jira Intake** view where a Toolbox user **drag-and-drops the exported `Jira-Intake.xlsx`/CSV** produced by the Teams "New Request" Power Automate flow, sees the parsed submissions in a newest-first queue, and creates Jira issues from them. Because the Teams submission contract is fixed, **mapping is by convention — nothing is typed**: `summary`, `description` (wiki markup), `priority` (by name), and **`issueType` (by name) all come from each row**; Acceptance Criteria goes to a configured custom field (default `customfield_10200`). The **only setting is the target project** (the one field not carried in the record) plus an **auto-create-on-import** toggle; settings persist in the shared Confluence content-property store. Each created issue sets the **reporter to the submitter** when their email resolves to a Jira user (new `searchUsers` wrapper using the Data Center `query`→`username` fallback), otherwise it falls back to the integration account (the `/jira-proxy` account). Dedup is **local by submission `id`** — re-importing the same or a superset file never double-creates. Submissions are parsed client-side with the bundled SheetJS parser (dynamically imported) and tolerate flat columns, dotted/nested keys, and extra columns. New `client/src/views/JiraIntake/` feature (lib + hooks + components) with co-located tests.
- **Teams → Jira intake — submitter origin never lost (feature 005, US2)**: When a submitter's email does not resolve to a Jira user (no match, ambiguous, or lookup error), the issue is still created under the integration account and a **wiki-markup origin note** ("Submitted via Teams by …") is **prepended to the description** so the request's origin is preserved. New pure `describeSubmitter` helper; the create flow prepends the note on the fallback path (into the configured description field, or as the description when none was provided).
- **Teams → Jira intake — review-and-pick queue (feature 005, US3)**: With the config's **auto-create toggle off**, importing a file creates nothing; instead each new submission shows **Create** and **Dismiss** actions in the queue, so a Toolbox user reviews and creates only the ones to move forward (created rows show their Jira key; dismissed rows become "Skipped"). Dedup still guarantees nothing is created twice. New `dismissEntry` on the queue hook and per-row review actions in the queue.
- **Teams → Jira intake — Home card (feature 005)**: Added a **Jira Intake** card to the Home view (Agile & Delivery section). Invalid issue types or priorities are surfaced as a clear per-row failure from Jira's own validation (the row shows Failed with the message) rather than being pre-guessed.
- **Teams → Jira intake — per-row project routing via project mapping (feature 005)**: The submission `project` column carries a **friendly project name** (e.g. "Cleanup Crew"); Intake settings include a **project-name → Jira-project-key mapping** (e.g. "Cleanup Crew" → `ENCUC`) so each row is created in the right Jira project. Rows with a blank project use the **default project**; a project name with no mapping is flagged **Invalid** with a clear reason (never created in the wrong project). The term **"project"** is used consistently across the Teams form, the Excel column, and Toolbox (the tenant reserves "team" for something else). New pure `resolveProjectKey` helper + mapping editor in the settings panel.
- **Teams → Jira intake — queue now shows every captured field (feature 005)**: The intake queue previously displayed only status, summary, submitter, timestamp, and Jira key, which made imports look like they had dropped data. It now shows the **description and acceptance criteria** (as detail lines under the summary) plus dedicated **Type**, **Priority**, and **Project** columns — all values were always parsed and used at create time; they just weren't displayed.

### Fixed
- **Teams → Jira intake — Save settings enables with a project mapping (no default project required)**: The Save button stayed disabled unless a default project was set, which blocked users who route every row via the project mapping. Save now enables when there is **either** a default project **or** at least one complete project mapping (the default project is only used for rows whose "project" column is blank).
- **Teams → Jira intake — manual create + per-row actions**: There was no way to create issues by hand or confirm a create worked. The queue now always shows per-row **Create**/**Dismiss** (and **Retry** on a failed row) once settings are saved, plus a **"Create N issues in Jira"** button above the queue for a manual bulk run — independent of the auto-create toggle. Rows flip to **Imported** with their Jira key on success or **Failed** with the Jira message, so the outcome is visible.

### Fixed
- **Teams → Jira intake — surface SharePoint errors + standardize on "Refresh" (feature 007/008 follow-up)**: A failed SharePoint read (e.g. a 403) now shows **SharePoint's own message and the request path** instead of a bare status code, so the cause (access denied, wrong site, missing list) is diagnosable. Standardized the SharePoint action label on **"Refresh from SharePoint"** (the app's convention for reloading from a source; it sits next to the existing "Auto-refresh" toggle) — replacing the one-off "Pull" wording.
- **Teams → Jira intake — SharePoint connect UX fixes + URL tolerance (feature 007 follow-up)**: The relay bookmarklet is now a proper **draggable install link** (`BookmarkletInstallLink`) with step-by-step instructions, instead of raw JavaScript shown in a text box. Removed the broken "Open SharePoint site" button (it navigated to the Toolbox home because only the site-relative path is stored). The **SharePoint site field now accepts a full site or list URL** pasted from the browser — Toolbox reduces it to the site-relative path (`/sites/CUCIntake`) and auto-fills the list name from a pasted list URL (new pure `parseSharePointListUrl`). *(A follow-up will move the relay connect into the unified Connection Bar.)*
- **My Issues "Today" tab — dark-theme formatting fixed**: The completed-duty cards, the "done for today" banner, and the Sprint-flow snapshot rendered as white/pale-green boxes in dark mode because their CSS referenced non-existent tokens (`--color-surface-alt`, `--color-success-bg`, `--color-success-text`, `--color-warning-bg`) that fell back to hard-coded light colors. They now use the app's real theme variables (`--color-surface`/`--color-surface-2`, a `color-mix` success tint, `--color-text-primary`, `--color-border-warning`), so the Today tab is readable and on-theme.
- **Mentions — issue links now open the real Jira issue (not the Toolbox home page)**: Clicking a mention's issue key bounced to the Toolbox home page because the base URL was read from a flat `config.jiraBaseUrl` that is always `undefined` (the `/api/proxy-config` response nests it under `jira.baseUrl`), so links fell back to a relative `/browse/KEY` the SPA router couldn't resolve. Mentions now reads the base URL via `fetchJiraBaseUrl()` and builds absolute Jira links. (Validated the other issue-link surfaces: Hygiene reads the connection store correctly, Defect Management and Business Helper use their own configured URLs — all fine. The Settings base-URL display has the same flat-read mismatch but is config display, not a link — noted for separate cleanup.)
- **Jira Template Maker — "ask every time" checkbox relabeled** to "Leave blank / fill in per use", which reads correctly for the shareable link (the literal per-use prompt only happens on the in-Toolbox create path); the optional-default hint was clarified.
- **Jira Template Maker — share link "base URL unavailable" fixed**: Copy link reported "Could not build the share link — the Jira base URL or project id is unavailable" because the client read a flat `config.jiraBaseUrl` from `/api/proxy-config`, but the endpoint actually returns it **nested as `jira.baseUrl`** (the `ProxyConfig` type was inaccurate), so the base URL was always empty. Added a correct `fetchJiraBaseUrl()` accessor that reads the real shape; the template maker now resolves the base URL and builds the prefill link. (The same latent mismatch affected the Mentions tab's base-URL read, which fell back to relative links.) Tests added; full client suite GREEN.
- **Jira Template Maker — "Copy link" now works and gives feedback**: Clicking Copy link on a saved template appeared to do nothing. Three causes: the confirmation message only rendered inside the Review step (so saved-template actions showed no feedback), the async Clipboard API can be blocked in the app's webview, and older saved templates had no stored `pid`. Now the status message is shown **globally** at the top of the view; clipboard copy uses a **`copyToClipboard` helper with an execCommand fallback** (and, if both fail, the message includes the raw link to copy manually); and Copy link **resolves the project id on demand** (`getProject`) for templates saved before pids were stored. The Review-step copy button also reports copied/failed states. New `copyToClipboard` helper + tests; full client suite GREEN (2494); build clean.

### Added
- **Jira Template Maker — shareable prefill links for NON-Toolbox users (primary output)**: Templates now generate a copyable **`CreateIssueDetails!init.jspa` prefill URL** (Jira Data Center) that opens Jira's native create screen pre-populated, so **anyone with Jira access can create the issue under their own session — no NodeToolbox needed**. This was the original intent of the feature. The link carries `pid` + `issuetype` + each templated field keyed by its Jira field id (choices by option id, labels repeated, text as wiki markup; prompt-at-launch fields contribute a default if set). It's copyable from the wizard's Review step and from each saved template ("Copy link"). For fields the API can't auto-map, a **manual field-mapping** editor lets the user append hand-mapped `param=value` pairs to the link (saved with the template). The numeric project id is resolved via `GET /rest/api/2/project/{key}` and the Jira base URL via `/api/proxy-config`. The in-Toolbox one-click create is retained as a bonus for Toolbox users. New pure `buildPrefillUrl` helper + `ShareLinkPanel` component; `getProject` wrapper; manual-mapping state. 99 feature tests GREEN; full client suite GREEN (2491); production build clean.

### Fixed
- **Jira Template Maker — project suggestion dropdown is now opaque/on-theme**: The project search suggestions rendered on a translucent surface (`--color-surface-2`/`--color-card-bg-subtle` are semi-transparent), so page content bled through and it didn't match the app's other dropdowns. It now uses the solid `--color-surface` background with a stronger border/shadow, matching the rest of the application's dark dropdowns.
- **Jira Template Maker — issue types now load (modern createmeta endpoints) and the project picker matches the app theme**: Two issues from first real use. (1) Selecting a project failed with "Could not load issue types…" because the tool used the **classic bulk `createmeta?projectKeys=` endpoint**, which Atlassian **removed on Jira Cloud and Data Center 10+**. The tool now uses the **modern createmeta endpoints** — `…/issuetypes` (issue types per project) and `…/issuetypes/{id}` (fields per issue type, loaded lazily on selection) — which work on Cloud and DC 8.4+. The create payload now identifies the project by **key** (no project-id lookup needed). When metadata still can't load, the error now includes the underlying status to aid diagnosis. (2) The project step's suggestion list used a native `<datalist>` (which renders an unthemeable white popup); it's now a **custom dark-themed combobox** consistent with the rest of the app, and the view's inputs use the app's real theme variables. New `getProjectIssueTypes`/`getIssueTypeFields` wrappers, `mapCreateMetaFieldList`, lazy field-loading in `useJiraCreateMeta`. Full client suite GREEN (2482); production build clean.

### Changed
- **Jira Template Maker — project step now searches by key, seeded with the ART's projects**: The project step no longer loads a full dropdown of every Jira project. It's a **searchable key input** whose type-ahead suggestions default to the **ART-configured projects** (the ART-wide `featureProjectKeys` filter, falling back to the configured team roster's project keys), while still letting you enter **any** project key directly. Keys are normalized to uppercase. New pure `getArtProjectKeys`/`mergeArtProjectKeys` helpers and an `ArtProjectInput` component (replaces `JiraProjectPicker` in this view only); 6 tests added, full client suite GREEN (2477), build clean.

### Added
- **Jira Template Maker — build & save templates (feature 004, US1)**: A new guided view (Home → 🧩 Jira Template Maker, route `/jira-template-maker`) that lets anyone build a reusable Jira issue template through dependent **Project → Issue Type → Field** pickers. Every choice is constrained by live Jira `createmeta`, so only real issue types, fields, and dropdown options are selectable and unsupported field types (e.g. cascading selects) are shown but not addable. Each field can be **fixed** or marked **ask-at-launch**; free-text fields get a core-formatting editor that emits Jira (Server/DC) wiki markup. Templates are **globally shared** — saved to a new `nodetoolbox-jira-templates` content property on the shared ART Confluence database with the author recorded (from `/myself`) and a 3-way merge guarding concurrent edits. A **Saved templates** list lets anyone launch a template and **create a real Jira issue in one confirmed action**: the launch dialog prompts only for fields marked ask-at-launch (pre-filling defaults), validates required fields before any POST (naming any that are missing and creating nothing), then creates the issue and shows an **open-in-Jira** link. Reporter is a normal templatable field; when unset the issue is created by the integration account, and the dialog says so. **Labels** are case-sensitive, de-duplicated, and labels Jira would reject (containing spaces) are flagged and excluded rather than silently dropped. Saved templates can be **edited and deleted** from the library; a template that references a field or option no longer present in Jira is **flagged as needing review and blocked from launch** (drift detection) so it can't create a malformed issue. Fields marked ask-at-launch may carry an optional default, and the step navigation prevents skipping prerequisites. Underpinned by tested, I/O-free helpers (`fieldModel`, `wikiMarkup`, `labels`, `buildCreatePayload`, `drift`, `requiredFields`, `browseUrl`) and new `jiraApi` (`getCreateMeta`/`createIssue`/`getMyself`) + `confluenceApi` (`loadJiraTemplates`/`saveJiraTemplates`/`mergeJiraTemplateStores`) functions. 80 unit/component tests added for the feature; full client suite GREEN; `tsc -b` and the production build clean; no regressions. The implementation is feature-complete pending **live-Jira quickstart validation** (the Article X proof gate — `specs/004-jira-template-maker/quickstart.md`), which requires a running Jira instance.

### Fixed
- **CHG Generator now sets the Planned start/end dates on created changes**: New change requests created from the CHG Generator left **Planned start date** and **Planned end date** empty in ServiceNow. Two defects compounded: (1) the create payload (`buildChangeRequestPayload` in `useCrgState.ts`) wrote the window to `planned_start_date`/`planned_end_date`, but on the `change_request` table those form fields are actually `start_date`/`end_date` (confirmed via the field inspector — `planned_*` only exist on `change_task`); and (2) the date value was sent in the HTML datetime-local shape (`2026-07-02T14:00`), not the `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` format ServiceNow's Table API expects for `glide_date_time` fields. ServiceNow's Table API silently drops both unknown field names *and* unparseable values on insert, so the dates were discarded. The payload now writes `start_date`/`end_date` (matching the read path in `useReleaseManagement.ts` and the modify-PATCH path in `api.js`), and a new pure helper `formatSnowDateTimeForApi` reformats every CHG and CTASK date to ServiceNow's canonical format. The wall-clock value is preserved as-typed (no timezone shift). Change-payload test assertions updated and 5 helper unit tests added; 361 SnowHub tests GREEN.
- **Scope/Feature change reports no longer blank the "previous value" when a field changed more than once in a self-healed window**: The coverage-watermark rework (v0.24.4) widened a report's look-back window from the prior business day to up to 30 days so downtime self-heals. But the change extractors still emitted one row per raw Jira changelog item, taking the "previous" column from that single item's `fromString`. When a field changed several times inside the widened window — e.g. an issue removed from one sprint and then added to another, or a Fix Version dropped then re-set — the last raw edit's `fromString` was empty, so the report showed `— → NewValue` even though the field genuinely held a prior value when the window opened. Both extractors (`scopeChangeScheduler.extractChangeEntries`, `featureChangeScheduler.extractFeatureChangeEntries`) now collapse all in-window edits to the same issue+field into a single **net** change: previous = the earliest change's value, current = the latest change's value. Single-change windows (normal daily operation) are unchanged. 2 tests added; 752 server tests GREEN.

### Changed
- **"Rovo" feature generalized to "AI Assist" (still gated behind Ctrl+Alt+Z; new passphrase)**: Every reference to the hidden "Rovo" capability is now "AI Assist" — UI labels and buttons, report panel titles (`🤖 AI Assist insight` / `🤖 AI Assist trend`), log messages, code identifiers (`useAiAssistStore`, `createAiAssistExchangeRouter`, `requestAiAssistText`, `parseAiAssistClassifications`, …), filenames (`aiAssistExchange.js`, `aiAssistEnrichment.js`, `aiAssistStore.ts`, `useAiAssist.ts`, `useAiAssistExchange.ts`, `AiAssistAutomationPanel.tsx`, `releaseAiAssistNotes.ts`), API routes (`/api/ai-assist/config` · `/dispatch` · `/result`), CSS classes, the gate's sessionStorage key (`tbxAiAssistUnlocked`), and the persisted config key (`rovoAutomation` → `aiAssistAutomation`). The config rename ships with a transparent on-load migration so existing installs keep their saved webhook/parking settings (the obfuscated `webhookSecret` is decoded correctly under the new key). The feature remains hidden behind the **Ctrl+Alt+Z** lockout, and the unlock passphrase is now **`ainow`** (stored only as a SHA-256 digest). No behaviour change. Two values are deliberately preserved to avoid breaking live data/integrations: the Confluence parking-page title prefix `rovo-result-` (an Atlassian Automation contract) and the `tbx-release-rovo-notes` localStorage key (so already-drafted release notes still load). Verified green: 215 client test files / 2326 tests, 52 server suites / 715 tests, `tsc` + production build clean.

### Added
- **My Issues — "Today" Scrum Master dashboard (deterministic daily checklist)**: My Issues now opens on a new **Today** tab — a single, at-a-glance landing page that mashes the data the product already pulls into one prioritized daily checklist for a Scrum Master. Eight category cards (respond to mentions, unblock issues, my stale issues, team stale issues, unassigned in-progress, sprint commitment gaps, due/overdue today, untriaged new issues) each show a live count and a one-click **deep link** to exactly where the work is done (My Issues sub-tabs, the Sprint Dashboard's Blockers/Hygiene tabs, or the DSU board). Counts are derived purely from the existing Hygiene rules and Mentions/Sprint sources, so the Today tab can never disagree with those surfaces — there is **no AI dependency**. Each card resolves independently (a slow or failing source never blanks its siblings), team-scope cards show an explicit "team not set up" state instead of a misleading zero, and a connection-required banner replaces the cards when Jira isn't connected. A per-card **daily check-off** persists per user and per business day (server-side `sm-checklist-state.json`) and **resets on the next working day** via `mostRecentBusinessDayKey` — a card auto-completes when its count hits zero, and when every duty is cleared the dashboard shows a "done for today" confirmation. An informational sprint-flow snapshot (WIP by status zone + days remaining) rounds it out. New `useTodayDashboard` and `useChecklistCompletion` hooks plus `CategoryCard` and `SprintFlowSnapshot` components; 23 tests added across the hooks and components — all GREEN; `tsc -b` + production build clean.
- **Report delivery is no longer a black box — Admin Hub shows each report's last run**: Every scheduled (and manual) Scope Change / Feature Change delivery now records its outcome — **delivered**, **skipped (no changes)**, or **error** — to a persistent `report-delivery-status.json` in AppData, and the Admin Hub Reports panels show a "Last run …" line under each team report and rollup. This was added because a stale Confluence page gave no clue whether the report *skipped because nothing changed* or *failed to update* — the outcome only ever went to the server console. New shared `src/services/reportDeliveryStatus.js` (records the outcome of each delivery, wraps both scheduled fires and the Admin Hub "Run Now"), new `GET /api/notifications/delivery-status` endpoint, and a per-row status line in the Admin Hub. 16 tests added (store + endpoint); all server + client suites GREEN.
- **Mentions report — issue key opens the ticket in Jira**: In My Issues → **Mentions**, each mention's issue key is now a link (with an ↗) that opens the real Jira issue in a new tab. This is needed because the inline reply box can't **@-mention** other people — opening the ticket in Jira lets you tag users in your response. The link is built from the configured Jira base URL (fetched via `/api/proxy-config`); if that's unavailable the report still loads and the key falls back to a relative `/browse/KEY` path. New pure `buildJiraBrowseUrl` helper; 7 tests added.
- **My Issues — "Mentions" report (reply to @-tags, mark them addressed)**: A new **Mentions** tab in My Issues finds the comments where you've been @-tagged within an adjustable business-day window (1 / 3 / 5 / 10, default 3, weekends excluded). Each hit is a card showing who tagged you, when, and an excerpt; expanding it opens the full ticket via the shared `IssueDetailPanel` so you can read the thread and **reply inline**. You can clear a mention two ways — a manual **Mark addressed** button, or automatically by posting a reply — and addressed mentions fall off the list (a "Show addressed" toggle reveals them with an **Undo**). "Addressed" is tracked **per individual mention** (a fresh tag on the same ticket re-surfaces) and stored **server-side** (new `mention-state.json` in AppData, namespaced per Jira user) so it follows you across browsers and survives restarts. Detection runs client-side through the existing Jira proxy: it reads `/rest/api/2/myself`, narrows candidates with a recent-activity JQL, then precisely matches `[~you]` wiki-markup and ADF mention nodes in each comment body. New server endpoints `GET/POST /api/mention-state`; new pure helpers for business-day windows and mention matching. 30 tests added across client + server — all GREEN.
- **Issue detail panel shows existing comments (Hygiene overview + everywhere)**: The expandable inline issue card now displays the issue's existing Jira comments — each with author, date, and plain-text body — in a read-only history above the "Add Comment" form. Comments are fetched on demand per expanded card (like the status transitions already are), so bulk issue lists stay lean. Posting a new comment refreshes the list in place. Because the change lives in the shared `IssueDetailPanel`, every consumer of it (Hygiene overview, Sprint Dashboard standup, My Issues, ART view) gains the comment history. 4 tests added (2300 client tests GREEN).
- **CHG Generator — clone-to-create flow**: The "Clone from existing CHG" control moved from the Workspace tools panel onto the **Fetch Issues** step, where it sits beside "By Project & Version" and "Custom JQL" as a third way to start. Cloning now reproduces the *whole* change: in addition to the header fields, `cloneFromChg` fetches **all** of the source CHG's change tasks (verbatim, regardless of state) into the staged CTASK list, defaults the "overwrite ServiceNow's auto-created CTASKs" option **on**, and jumps straight to **Step 6 (Review & Create)** — because cloning is reproducing a change, not templating. Steps 2–5 stay editable via the step badges. The Workspace panel is now "Templates & Defaults". 4 tests added (355 SnowHub tests GREEN).
- **Sprint Release — Workflow Topology Validator**: New `GET /api/sprint-release/workflow-topology` endpoint queries Jira in parallel for each configured project's issue types, statuses, the sub-status custom field's allowed option values (via `createmeta`), and the dev project's available workflow transitions (via a sample issue). Returns a structured topology with per-project reachability and a `validation` block showing whether each configured rule value (`qeHandoffSubStatusValue`, `btHandoffSubStatusValue`, `doneTransitionName`) actually exists in the live Jira instance. A new "Validate Workflow" button in the Sprint Release Admin Hub panel calls the endpoint and renders the `WorkflowTopologyCard` — project columns with issue types and status lists, sub-status options highlighted where they match the configured triggers, transitions with the configured Done transition highlighted, and a colour-coded validation summary (✓ / ✗ per rule). 19 tests added, 702 total — all GREEN.
- **Fix stale Rovo gate guard**: Removed leftover `activeAdminTab === 'hygiene-monitor'` comparison that caused a TypeScript build error after Hygiene Monitor was moved to Reports Config.
- **Admin Hub UI — Sprint Release panel, Hygiene Monitor in Reports Config, UX polish**: Sprint Release gets a dedicated visible Admin Hub tab with a full config form and live runtime status card. Hygiene Monitor moves from the Rovo-gated hidden tab into Reports Config as a third sub-tab alongside Scope Change and Feature Change. New Hygiene tab in Reports Hub runs on-demand per-team scans with inline results. Rovo Automation and Hygiene Monitor forms now use the correct `fieldRow` / `fieldLabel` / `textInput` layout — labels separated from inputs with proper vertical gap matching the Scope Change style.
- **Sprint–Release Workflow Orchestrator (feature 003 — complete)**: Adds the Jira Sprint–Release Workflow Orchestrator that automates dev-issue Done transitions, QE/BT handoff comments, sprint–FixVersion date sync, defect intake (label-triggered new issues), and Definition of Ready violation gate. New files: `src/services/sprintReleaseOrchestrator.js` (pure business logic), `src/services/sprintReleaseScheduler.js` (polling loop, ring buffers), `src/routes/sprintRelease.js` (5 REST endpoints). The `sprintRelease.teamProfiles` config block is persisted via `src/config/loader.js`. The scheduler starts on server boot. 63 tests added (52 unit + 11 integration) — all GREEN. All 7 Quickstart Scenarios from `specs/003-sprint-release-workflow/quickstart.md` covered by the integration test suite.
- **Rovo trend paragraph on the ART-rollup reports too (US1 completion)**: The aggregate cross-team ART-rollup variants of the scope-change and feature-change reports now also prepend a non-blocking Rovo trend paragraph above the rollup table, identifying which team/release is most at risk across the ART. Same pattern and guarantees as the per-team reports: gated by `rovoAutomation.isEnabled`, skipped silently (with a logged reason) when Rovo is unavailable so the rollup always publishes. This finishes US1 — all four scheduled-report surfaces (standup, scope per-team + rollup, feature per-team + rollup) are now Rovo-enriched.
- **Hygiene Monitor shows a per-team violation trend (SC-009)**: The Hygiene Monitor panel now displays a trend indicator beside each team's violation count — **↓ improving**, **↑ worsening**, or **→ unchanged** — once at least two scans have run (hidden on a team's first scan). The trend is computed by the scan's existing digest, cached with the result, and returned from `GET /api/hygiene-monitor/status`; the panel renders it. Completes the last open US3 acceptance item.
- **Hygiene monitor config field rename — implementation aligned with data model**: Server-side config encode/decode (`src/config/loader.js`), route secret-scrubbing (`src/routes/hygieneMonitor.js`), Admin Hub panel interface + form labels (`client/src/views/AdminHub/HygieneMonitorPanel.tsx`), and all test fixtures have been renamed from the initial `teamsWebhookUrl`/`teamsWebhookSecret` field names to the canonical `digestTriggerUrl`/`digestTriggerSecret`/`digestEmailTo` names specified in `specs/002-rovo-expansion-hygiene-monitor/data-model.md`. No behaviour change — the delivery mechanism (Atlassian Automation trigger webhook → email → inbox rule → Teams) was always as described in the entries below.
- **Hygiene digest is delivered by email, not a Teams webhook (US3 reconciliation)**: The proactive hygiene monitor now emails its digest by firing a trigger webhook to an Atlassian Automation rule that composes the email (the recipient's inbox rule forwards it into Teams), matching how the other reports already work. Per-team config keys are `digestTriggerUrl` / `digestTriggerSecret` (base64-obfuscated) / `digestEmailTo`. Because the destination is now an Atlassian Automation host, the previous Microsoft Teams allow-list exception (`.webhook.office.com`) was **removed** from `webhookHostPolicy.js`, so all outbound webhooks are Atlassian-only again. (Supersedes the Teams-webhook wording in the US3 entries below.)
- **Hygiene monitor UI panels (T032/T033/T034)**: Two passphrase-gated panels complete the US3 front-end. In **Admin Hub → 🧹 Hygiene Monitor** (T032), operators configure per-team settings: project keys, daily schedule time, weekday checkboxes, and Teams incoming webhook URL/secret (write-only from the UI). A "Scan Now" button triggers an immediate run and shows the result inline. In the **Hygiene view** (T033), a status panel shows the last-scan time and per-team violation counts with a "Scan Now" trigger. Both panels are hidden until the Ctrl+Alt+Z Rovo gate is unlocked (`isRovoUnlocked === true`); re-locking automatically switches the Admin Hub back to the Config tab. The Hygiene Monitor tab appears beside the existing ⚡ Rovo tab when unlocked (T034). All 11 new tests pass.
- **Hygiene monitor scheduler boot (T030)**: `startHygieneMonitorScheduler` wired in `server.js` alongside the other three schedulers. Fires every 60 seconds; per-team schedule-time + weekday guards prevent duplicate runs within the same day. "Scan Now" via the route bypasses the daily guard.
- **Hygiene monitor scan engine (T025-T029)**: `runHygieneScan` now orchestrates a full scan: queries Jira for open issues, evaluates all 20 hygiene rules per issue, batches violations into Rovo classification prompts (50 violations/batch, non-blocking), applies FIXABLE field updates via the Jira proxy (rejected updates are re-classified as UNFIXABLE), posts UNFIXABLE comments with per-cycle dedup (one comment per issue+checkId pair per run), builds a trend digest, and emails it via the team's Atlassian Automation digest webhook (`reportWebhookDelivery`). A `hygiene-digest` surface is registered in `reportSurfaceRegistry.js` and resolves the destination (`digestTriggerUrl`/`digestTriggerSecret`) from `configuration.hygieneMonitor.teams`. (See the reconciliation note above — the earlier Teams-host exception was removed.)
- **Hygiene monitor config persistence (T024)**: The `hygieneMonitor` section is now saved to and loaded from `toolbox-proxy.json`. Each team's `digestTriggerSecret` is base64-obfuscated on disk (same pattern as other credentials) and never appears in API responses. Scan history is bounded to the 30 most recent entries (one month of daily scans). The config survives restarts and version upgrades.
- **Proactive hygiene monitor foundation (US3 of the Rovo-expansion feature)**: Adds the server-side building blocks for the daily hygiene scan pipeline. `src/services/hygieneRules.js` is a dependency-free CommonJS port of the 20 client-side hygiene predicates, sharing the same check IDs and severity levels. `src/services/hygieneMonitorScheduler.js` exports `parseRovoClassifications(text)` (parses Rovo's `FIXABLE: KEY | field | value` / `UNFIXABLE: KEY | checkId | guidance` lines, skips malformed rows) and `buildHygieneDigest(scan, priorScan)` (computes violation trend: up/down/flat/n-a). `src/routes/hygieneMonitor.js` provides the router factory for `GET/POST /api/hygiene-monitor/config`, `POST /api/hygiene-monitor/scan`, and `GET /api/hygiene-monitor/status`; secrets are scrubbed from every response. The scan engine, Jira fix application, Teams digest delivery, Admin Hub panel, and Hygiene view panel follow in subsequent increments (T024–T034).
- **Rovo-assisted CHG drafting and risk check in the wizard (US2 of the Rovo-expansion feature)**: Adds two optional, passphrase-gated Rovo accelerators to the CHG Creation Wizard. In **Step 3 (Change Details)**, a "Draft with Rovo" button (visible only when the Ctrl+Alt+Z gate is unlocked) dispatches the selected Jira issues to Rovo and writes the returned Short Description and Description into the CHG state — both fields remain fully editable and the button is non-blocking (wizard proceeds without it). In **Step 6 (Review & Create)**, a "Risk check with Rovo" button sends the CHG payload to Rovo for a pre-submission gap review; identified gaps are rendered inline and submission is never blocked by the result (FR-004/FR-005/SC-007).
- **Rovo enrichment on scheduled reports (US1 of the Rovo-expansion feature)**: Implements Story A of spec `002-rovo-expansion-hygiene-monitor`. Adds a shared, non-blocking server-side Rovo helper (`requestRovoText` in `src/services/rovoEnrichment.js`) that dispatches a prompt and polls for the result via the existing exchange, returning `null` (never throwing) on disable/timeout/error so report delivery is never blocked. All three scheduled-report surfaces now prepend a Rovo block above their tables when Rovo is enabled: an **insight block** on standup briefings, and a **trend-commentary paragraph** (identifying the release most at risk) on scope-change and feature-change reports. When Rovo is unavailable, every report publishes unchanged with a logged skip — delivery is never blocked (FR-001/FR-002/SC-008). Applies to the per-team reports; the aggregate ART-rollup variants and the CHG-wizard actions + proactive hygiene monitor are subsequent increments of the same feature.
- **Reconcile linked CTASKs with ServiceNow's auto-created ones (per CHG template)**: A new per-CHG-template toggle, "Update ServiceNow's auto-created CTASKs to match these (then create the rest)", changes how linked CTASKs are written on CHG create. When on, NodeToolbox reads the CTASKs ServiceNow auto-generated for the new change and **updates them in place, paired by list order** (1st linked → 1st auto-created, etc.), then **creates new records only for staged CTASKs beyond the auto-created count** — so teams whose change process auto-spawns CTASKs don't get duplicates. It detects however many were auto-created (not a fixed number) and polls briefly so an async ServiceNow workflow can't cause a miss. When off (default), behaviour is unchanged: the existing team-specific auto-CTASK rename runs and all staged CTASKs are created new. The toggle is saved on the CHG template alongside its CTASK links.
- **Link CTASK templates to a CHG template and auto-stage them on apply**: A CHG template can now remember a set of linked CTASK templates. In the CRG workspace, a new "Linked CTASKs" checklist (under CHG Templates) lets you tick which saved CTASK templates belong to a CHG template; saving or updating the CHG template stores those links. Applying that CHG template now auto-stages the linked CTASKs into the change-task list (pre-filled but still editable), so you create the CHG and all its CTASKs in one batch instead of adding each CTASK by hand in the final step. Re-applying the same template doesn't stack duplicates, and a linked template you've since deleted is skipped. Existing CHG templates without links are unaffected. (Cloning a CTASK from ServiceNow into a template already existed; this connects those templates to the CHG flow.)

### Fixed
- **Scope/Feature Change reports self-heal missed days (window follows the last run, not a fixed prior business day)**: The reports looked back to the *previous business day*, which silently assumed they ran and wrote every prior day. If the server was down on the day that would have reported a change, that change fell into a permanent gap — never written, even though it was genuinely new since the page was last updated (the Reports Hub's wider window still showed it). Each report now keeps a persisted **coverage watermark** (`report-coverage.json` in AppData) advanced on every confirmed run — a delivery *or* a skip (which confirms there was nothing to report), but **not** an error. The next run's cutoff is the prior business day **or** the last run, whichever is earlier (capped at a 30-day lookback) — so a downtime gap self-heals on the next run. Normal daily operation is unchanged: when a report runs every day its watermark is ~yesterday, so the window equals the prior business day exactly as before (Monday still covers Friday). Applies to both per-team reports and ART rollups, Scope and Feature Change. This is "start fresh from today" — the watermark begins at the first run after install, so there is no one-time backlog dump. 14 tests added (pure resolver + watermark store).
- **AI Assist can no longer stall a report by ~60 seconds**: AI Assist (formerly Rovo) enriches reports by dispatching a prompt to an Atlassian Automation webhook and then polling a Confluence "parking page" for the answer. With **Rovo turned off, nothing ever writes that page**, so every report waited the full poll budget (20 × 3 s ≈ **60 s**) before giving up — adding a minute and ~20 noise lines to every run while producing no enrichment. The default budget is cut from **60 s → ~6 s** (3 × 3 s), so a dead or slow backend costs seconds, not a minute; report delivery is otherwise unchanged, and a future Copilot-backed setup can still pass a larger `pollAttempts`. (Disabling `aiAssistAutomation.isEnabled` in the Admin Hub remains the way to skip the attempt entirely.) Test added pinning the bounded default.
- **Scheduled Scope Change report now matches the Reports Hub (Sprint changes + all issue types)**: The scheduled/Admin-Hub Scope Change report queried only `issuetype = Feature AND fixVersion changed`, so it silently skipped **Sprint changes** and any change on a **Story/Task** — even though the Reports Hub (and the original report) showed them. A report that had a real sprint change (e.g. a Story moved to a new sprint) delivered *"skipped — no changes"* and the Confluence page never updated. The scheduler now runs the same two queries the Reports Hub does — `fixVersion changed` (all issue types) **and** `updated >=` filtered for Sprint-field changes — renders both a **📦 Release Changes** and a **🏃 Sprint Changes** section (per-team and ART rollup), delivers when *either* has data, and includes `sprintChangeCount` in the webhook. The prior-business-day window is unchanged (Monday still covers Friday). 5 tests added; server suite GREEN.
- **"Last run" line now always shows on each report row**: The delivery-status line added in v0.24.0 only rendered once a report had actually run, so a freshly-updated install showed nothing — looking like the feature was missing. Each Scope/Feature Change report row and rollup now always shows the line, reading **"Last run: not yet recorded"** until the first scheduled or manual run populates it.

### Changed
- **Feature Review hygiene fixes — one "Save all fixes" button, no more refresh-after-every-field**: In Team Dashboard → Feature Review, the "Direct hygiene fixes" panel previously had a Save button on every field and reloaded the entire feature rollup after each one (collapsing the panel and losing your place). It now has a single **Save all fixes** button that applies every field you've filled in — summary, dates, PI, application, fix version, assignee, story points, status transition — in one batch and refreshes **once**, at the end. A partial failure keeps the panel open with the failed fields' drafts intact and per-field error messages so you can retry just those; it only reloads when the whole batch succeeds. New multi-field batch test added; FeatureReviewTab suite GREEN (8 tests).
- **Scope/Feature Change report titles now stamp the latest update date**: When a report updates its ongoing Confluence page, the page title now reads `… — <YYYY-MM-DD>` reflecting the **most recent** run, instead of keeping the original create-date (or an undated title). Confluence simply renames the page to the new date on each update, so the title always tells you when it was last refreshed. Applies to both per-team reports and the ART rollups, for Scope Change and Feature Change.

### Fixed
- **Scheduled reports now survive a restart and catch up on a missed slot**: Every report scheduler (Scope Change, Feature Change, Standup Briefing, Hygiene Monitor) previously fired only on an *exact* HH:MM minute match and tracked "already fired today" **in memory only**. If the server was not running during that precise minute — a restart, a late start, or a busy event loop — the slot passed un-checked and that day's report was silently skipped; an in-memory tracker also meant a restart lost all knowledge of what had already fired. Two changes fix this: (1) a new shared persistent store `src/services/schedulerFiredState.js` writes each scheduler's last-fired dates to `scheduler-fired-state.json` in AppData (alongside `toolbox-proxy.json`), hydrated into each scheduler when it starts on boot; and (2) the fire condition changed from exact equality to **"scheduled time reached or passed today, and not already fired today"** (`isScheduledTimeReached`). A scheduler that starts late now still delivers the day's report, while the persisted fired-state prevents a restart from re-delivering a report that already went out. The Hygiene Monitor's old in-memory `Set` + manual day-rollover reset was replaced by the same date-keyed persistent map (the day rollover is now implicit in the date comparison). 12 store tests added; all 440 server tests + 117 co-located scheduler tests GREEN.
- **Release Notes PNG export crashed on modern CSS color functions**: Exporting (or copying) the Team Dashboard Release Notes section as a PNG threw *"Attempting to parse an unsupported color function 'color'"* and produced no image. The section's styling uses `color-mix(in srgb, …)`, which Chromium serialises through `getComputedStyle` as `color(srgb …)` notation — neither of which html2canvas 1.4.1 (the latest published release) can parse. A new `client/src/utils/colorFunctionFallback.ts` pre-pass now walks the cloned export subtree before capture and rewrites any `color-mix()`/`color()`/`oklch()` (and related) value into the equivalent `rgb()`/`rgba()` string the browser itself computes — flattening each colour via a 1×1 canvas read — so html2canvas only ever sees values it understands. The fix lives in the shared `downloadElementImage` utility, so every image export (not just Release Notes) is covered, and the panel's own background colour is flattened the same way. 9 tests added.
- **Release Notes import rejected AI responses that wrapped the JSON in chatter**: The Release Notes importer only accepted clean raw JSON or a single ` ```json ` fence — the exact shape Rovo returned. Copilot (the replacement now that Rovo is disabled) routinely adds a greeting, a sign-off, or a bare ` ``` ` fence around the payload, and any of those made the parse fail with *"Rovo response is not valid JSON."* `extractJsonPayload` in `releaseRovoNotes.ts` now also reads bare (untagged) code fences and narrows the payload to the outermost `{ … }`, discarding any prose before or after the object. The generated prompt was also tightened to instruct the assistant to emit the JSON object only, with no surrounding text or code fence. 3 tests added.
- **Team Dashboard Hygiene tab showed a previous team's data and missed stale issues assigned to teammates**: Two root causes. (1) The embedded Hygiene tab received the team's project key only through a `localStorage` side-channel: `TeamDashboardHygieneTab` wrote the key in a `useEffect`, but `useHygieneState` read it once in a mount-time `useState` initializer — which React runs *before* the parent's effect — so after switching teams the freshly-mounted Hygiene view initialised to the *previous* team's project and queried stale data. The project key now flows through a `projectKey` prop that is the authoritative source of truth (derived during render, not synced via an effect), so switching teams immediately re-scopes Hygiene; the `localStorage` seed remains only for the standalone view and is no longer written from the team tab. (2) In team mode the Hygiene query filtered by `assignee = currentUser()` (or a non-team-scoped global roster), while the dashboard's own issue list is not assignee-filtered — so stale issues that were unassigned or owned by teammates appeared on the dashboard but never in the Hygiene report. Hygiene now drops the assignee filter in team mode (via a nullable `assigneeClause`), auditing every in-scope issue exactly as the dashboard does. Standalone Hygiene is unchanged (still current-user scoped). 6 tests added/updated.
- **CHG clone dropped planning-tab values stored under instance-specific field names**: Cloning a CHG read each Planning assessment field (impact, availability impact, tested, impacted-persons-aware, performed-previously, success probability, can-be-backed-out) and the plan text areas from a single hard-coded ServiceNow column. But the submit path writes every field to *all* of its known aliases, and which column physically exists varies by instance — so on instances using the non-default alias the values read back empty and silently dropped. `cloneFromChg` now reads planning assessment and content through the same alias lists (`PLANNING_ASSESSMENT/CONTENT_ALIAS_FIELD_NAMES_BY_STATE_KEY`) the submit and verify paths use, via new `buildClonedPlanningAssessment`/`buildClonedPlanningContent` helpers, taking the first populated alias. Impacted-persons-aware (which also seeds the environment cards) is resolved the same way. 1 test added.
- **Team Dashboard Hygiene tab under-counted stale issues vs the Blockers tab**: The Hygiene "Stale" check hard-coded a 14-day threshold with a strict `>` comparison, while the Blockers tab uses the team's configurable `staleDaysThreshold` (default 5 days) with an inclusive `>=`. As a result a team with stale work showing in Blockers could still see a 100% Hygiene score with 0 stale issues. `checkStaleIssue` now accepts a `staleDaysThreshold` (defaulting to 14 for the standalone view) and uses an inclusive comparison, and `useHygieneState` feeds it the same `staleDaysThreshold` from the dashboard config the Blockers tab reads — so both surfaces agree on what counts as stale. 4 tests added.
- **Rovo result lookup parsed the Confluence response one level too shallow (the real bug)**: `fetchResult` read the parking page as `response.body.storage.value`, but `makeConfluenceApiRequest` wraps every response in a `{ status, body: <Confluence JSON> }` envelope, so the page content actually lives at `response.body.body.storage.value` (exactly how the working schedulers read it). The reader therefore always saw an empty body and the by-ID lookup reported `0B`/`no marker` regardless of the page, space, or editor — which sent earlier diagnosis chasing personal-space search, ADF, drafts, and live docs. Both the by-ID and title/space-search paths now unwrap the envelope correctly, and the unit tests were corrected to mirror the real `{ status, body }` shape (the old mocks returned the un-enveloped object and hid the bug).
- **Rovo result lookup now reads pages authored in the modern (ADF) editor**: A parking page created/edited in Confluence's modern editor returns an EMPTY `body.storage` over the REST API even though it visibly has content, so the by-ID read saw `raw=0B` and never matched — the round-trip timed out despite the rule writing the result correctly. The reader now also requests the rendered `body.view` and falls back to it when `body.storage` is blank, and the HTML stripper handles rendered markup (block tags and `&nbsp;`). The diagnostic log now reports `source=storage|view` and both body lengths, so an empty-in-both case (an unpublished draft) is still distinguishable.

### Changed
- **Release Notes report — copy to clipboard (table + image), neutral heading**: The rendered release-notes report now has a **"📋 Copy Release Notes"** action that copies the section to the clipboard instead of downloading a PNG file, with a brief "Copied to clipboard" confirmation (excluded from the captured image). The copy writes **two representations in one clipboard item**: a self-contained, inline-styled **HTML table** (so Outlook/Gmail paste a readable, reflowable native table that stays legible at email width) and a high-resolution **PNG image** (fallback for chat tools like Teams/Slack that only accept images). The report heading no longer says "Rovo Release Notes Draft" — it is now built from the dashboard **team name** and the release **fix version**, e.g. *"Transformers 06/23/2026 Release Notes"* (or *"06/23/2026 Release Notes"* when no team is set), so the report carries no mention of how the notes were drafted. New `buildReleaseNotesHeading` / `buildReleaseNotesHtml` helpers in `releaseRovoNotes.ts` (HTML values are escaped) and a `copyElementReportToClipboard` writer in `downloadElementImage.ts`; `ReleasesTab` now receives the active team name. 13 tests added/updated; the dual-format clipboard path (text/html + image/png written and read back) verified end-to-end in a real browser.
- **Rovo result lookup logs a snippet of the page it read when no marker matches**: When the by-ID parking-page read finds no matching correlationId, it now also logs the raw + stripped body lengths and the first 300 characters of the page text (`[Rovo] page <id> read: raw=…B stripped=…B snippet="…"`). This shows whether the page is empty over the API, returns unexpected markup, or simply lacks the marker — diagnosing the "visible in the editor but absent over the API" case directly.
- **Rovo result-lookup log now shows what it wants vs what the page holds**: When "Run via Rovo (auto)" times out, the result poll now logs `want=<correlationId> page-has=[<ids on the page>] match=true/false` for the by-ID parking page. An empty `page-has=[none]` means NodeToolbox is reading a different page than the rule writes to (wrong **Parking Page ID**); a different id in `page-has` means the page holds only a stale/previous run. This pinpoints a page-ID mismatch versus a stale result without guesswork.

### Fixed
- **Rovo parking page read now handles an "append" rule and ignores stale runs**: When the Confluence Automation rule uses "Append content to the end of a page" (rather than replacing it), the parking page accumulates one result block per run. The reader now isolates the block belonging to the current `correlationId` — the lines between this request's `correlationId:` marker and the next marker (or end of page) — instead of returning the whole accumulated page. A re-run with the same id supersedes its earlier block. This prevents a previous run's result from leaking into a new request and lets the static parking page work with either an append or a replace rule.

### Added
- **Rovo result lookup now uses a fixed "parking page" read by ID**: Searching for a per-run page by title never returns results in a personal ("~") Confluence space, so "Run via Rovo (auto)" kept timing out. The exchange now supports a single, reusable parking page that the Automation rule **edits** each run. NodeToolbox reads it directly by page ID (`GET /wiki/rest/api/content/<id>`) — a direct lookup that bypasses the search index and works in personal spaces. The rule stamps `correlationId: <id>` into the page body; NodeToolbox only accepts the result when that marker matches the current request (so a stale page reads as not-ready) and strips the marker line before parsing. Configure it in Admin Hub → ⚡ Rovo → **Parking Page ID**; the by-title space search remains as a fallback when no Page ID is set.

### Fixed
- **Rovo result lookup now finds pages in a personal Confluence space**: Confluence's `?spaceKey=~personal&title=` content search does not reliably return pages in a personal ("~") space, so the parking page was never found and "Run via Rovo (auto)" always timed out. Since the parking page title is a unique id, the lookup now tries a **global title search** and falls back to **listing the space's pages**, matching the exact title in code. Each attempt is logged (`[Rovo] result lookup [strategy] … → N page(s), MATCH/no match`) for diagnosis.

### Changed
- **Rovo exchange waits longer for the result**: The "Run via Rovo (auto)" poll window was ~60s (40 × 1.5s), which could expire before Rovo finished generating and Confluence indexed the new parking page — so a working round-trip looked like a timeout. The default is now ~3 minutes (60 × 3s). A successful run still returns as soon as the page is found.

### Fixed
- **Dev Panel → Server Logs was always empty**: The Dev Panel client filters log entries by a numeric `id` (`entry.id > lastSeenId`), but the server's log buffer wrote entries as `{ level, message, timestamp }` with no `id`, so every entry failed the filter and the panel showed nothing. The log buffer now assigns a monotonic `id` to each entry, so Server Logs populate as expected (and the `[Rovo] result lookup` diagnostics become visible).
- **Rovo automation config now persists across restarts and upgrades**: The config loader rebuilds `toolbox-proxy.json` from a fixed set of sections on every save and never included `rovoAutomation`, so the Rovo webhook URL / secret / parking space had to be re-entered after every restart or update. The loader now writes and reads `rovoAutomation` (with the webhook secret base64-obfuscated like other credentials), and the config lives in `%APPDATA%\NodeToolbox\`, so it survives version upgrades — regardless of whether the hidden panel is displayed.

### Changed
- **Rovo result lookup now logs its query**: The Rovo exchange's result poll logs the exact Confluence space + page title it searches for and how many pages matched (`[Rovo] result lookup: space=… title=… → N match(es)`), and logs the error if the Confluence request fails. Surfaces space/title mismatches in Dev Panel → Server Logs when a "Run via Rovo (auto)" times out.

### Fixed
- **Webhook host allow-list now accepts all Atlassian hosts**: The outbound webhook allow-list (used by report delivery and the Rovo exchange) only permitted `automation.atlassian.com` and `*.atlassian.net`, so a real Atlassian Automation webhook on `api-private.atlassian.com` was rejected with "Destination host is not an allowed Atlassian host; nothing was sent." The allow-list now permits any `*.atlassian.com` or `*.atlassian.net` host (still exact dot-suffix matched, so look-alikes like `evil-atlassian.com.attacker.com` remain rejected).
- **Scope Change scheduler — Sprint Changes section removed**: The Scope Change report now only surfaces PI-level Fix Version changes on Feature-type issues. The Sprint Changes section (and its supporting `fetchSprintChangeCandidates` query) has been removed entirely, so the ART rollup no longer writes "Team Summary / Release Changes / Sprint Changes" to the same Confluence page as the Feature Change report. The fix version JQL now also filters to `issuetype = Feature` so Story-level changes cannot appear.
- **Both schedulers — webhook fires only when there is real data**: The automation webhook (which drives email notifications) is already guarded by a data check; the sprint removal closes the remaining gap where a sprint-only run could trigger the webhook with zero release changes, producing a notification with no meaningful content.
- **Both schedulers — business-day aware window**: The look-back window is no longer a fixed 24-hour rolling period. Each run now computes the start of the previous business day (Mon → Friday midnight, Tue–Fri → yesterday midnight) so Monday's run captures everything that changed since Friday, and no run ever re-reports the same day twice due to time-of-day drift.
- **Both schedulers — weekend skip**: `checkAndFireScheduledReports` now exits immediately on Saturday and Sunday. The reports were never intended to run on non-business days; the missing guard could cause spurious weekend runs when the server stayed up over the weekend.

### Changed
- **Internal — Rovo unlock works from anywhere + toggles to re-hide**: The hidden Ctrl+Alt+Z shortcut now works from **any Admin Hub tab** (the listener moved to the Admin Hub root) and **toggles**: it opens the passphrase gate when locked and **re-hides all Rovo features when already unlocked**. The same toggle-to-hide behaviour was added to every generator surface (Create Change, risk, pointing, release), so Ctrl+Alt+Z re-hides from anywhere. When unlocked, a dedicated **⚡ Rovo** tab appears in Admin Hub holding the configuration form (it disappears again on re-hide); the config no longer lives under the Standup tab.
- **Internal — unified Rovo unlock + in-place Admin Hub unlock**: The Rovo capability unlock is now a single shared state (`rovoStore`) across every surface. The risk-refinement, release-notes, and story-pointing generators previously each kept their own per-surface unlock flag (`tbx-risk-rovo-unlocked`, `tbx-release-rovo-unlocked`, `tbx-pointing-rovo-unlocked`); those are removed and all now read the shared store, so one passphrase entry unlocks every Rovo affordance and the Admin Hub config section together. The Admin Hub "Rovo Automation" section now also responds to the hidden Ctrl+Alt+Z passphrase shortcut, so it can be unlocked and configured in place without first unlocking on another surface.

### Added
- **Internal — Rovo Automation config + remaining generators**: A passphrase-gated "⚡ Rovo Automation" section in Admin Hub now configures the Rovo webhook URL/secret and the Confluence parking space (`GET`/`POST /api/rovo/config`), with a Test action. The automated "Run via Rovo (auto)" exchange is now wired into all four hidden Rovo generators — CHG drafting, **release notes**, **risk refinement**, and **story pointing** — each reusing its existing prompt builder and response parser through the shared exchange. (Note: there is no Rovo generator for PRB.)
- **Internal — automated Rovo exchange (CHG)**: The hidden CHG drafting assistant can now run its deterministic prompt automatically instead of via manual copy-paste. A "Run via Rovo (auto)" action dispatches the generated prompt to a configured Atlassian Automation/Rovo webhook, polls for the deterministic response from a Confluence parking page keyed by a correlation id (write → read → delete), and applies the parsed `SHORT_DESCRIPTION/DESCRIPTION/JUSTIFICATION/RISK_AND_IMPACT` values to the matching CHG fields. The webhook destination is restricted to Atlassian hosts; the prompt is not redacted (the content is what Rovo must process). The capability stays behind the existing passphrase gate, and the unlock is now shared app-wide via a `rovoStore` so one passphrase entry covers every Rovo affordance. Requires a configured Rovo automation endpoint + parking space (`configuration.rovoAutomation`).

### Changed
- **Internal — test coverage backfill**: Added unit tests for the scope-change and feature-change schedulers (pure changelog-parsing, XML escaping, page-id extraction, and time helpers), the notifications and standup-briefing routes (config sanitisation, validation, and run/test endpoints), the admin unlock store, and the Admin Hub Pre-Standup Briefing panel. The two scheduler modules now also export their pure helpers so they can be unit-tested directly; no runtime behaviour changed.

### Fixed
- **SnowHub — Create Change Configuration tab no longer crashes on an unset reference field**: Opening the SnowHub Create Change Configuration tab threw `Cannot read properties of undefined` when a reference-type field had no value yet, because the CRG field-pin helpers (`serializePinnedFieldValue`, `canPinFieldValue`) assumed a populated `{ sysId, displayName }` reference. Both now guard `null`/`undefined` values, so an unset reference serialises to a stable non-matching key and is reported as not pinnable.

### Added
- **Report Webhook Delivery — "Send to Automation" on report surfaces**: The Standup Briefing, Scope Change report, and Feature Change report each gain a one-click "Send to Automation" action beside their existing copy button. It delivers the on-screen report to that team's existing Atlassian Automation webhook (the same per-team `triggerUrl`/`triggerSecret` already used by the scheduled reports), removing the manual copy-paste step. Delivery is server-mediated so the webhook secret never reaches the browser. The report is wrapped in a `payloadContext` envelope (`source`, `team`, `generatedAt`, `report`, `meta`) so an Atlassian Automation rule — including an inline "Use Rovo agent" step — can address fields via `{{webhookData.payloadContext.*}}` smart values. The manual clipboard copy remains available on every surface.
- **Report Webhook Delivery — security posture**: Destinations are validated against an Atlassian-hosts allow-list (`automation.atlassian.com` / `*.atlassian.net`, HTTPS only; look-alike hosts are rejected) — a non-Atlassian host is refused before any bytes are sent. Report content is scanned for credential patterns (bearer tokens, `password=`, Atlassian API tokens, basic-auth URLs) and any matches are redacted before sending, with the user notified how many values were redacted. HTTP status codes are logged; secrets never appear in logs.
- **Docs — `docs/automation-mappings.md`**: Auto-generated (`scripts/generate-automation-mappings.js`) from the report surface registry. For each surface it documents the exact JSON payload shape and a ready-to-paste Rovo "Use Rovo agent" System Prompt template.

### Added
- **Team Dashboard → Standup → Briefing mode**: A new "📋 Briefing" button in the Standup tab's mode toggle scans Jira activity for the current team's project key and renders a structured pre-standup briefing inline. The briefing buckets the last N days of changes (1–3, selectable) into Status Changes, Blockers, Defects, Risks, and Completions as plain-text markdown tables. A counts bar summarises each bucket at a glance and a "Copy Briefing" button puts the full text on the clipboard for pasting into Slack, Teams, or a stand-up doc.
- **Admin Hub — Pre-Standup Briefing**: Scheduled delivery of the same briefing via Confluence blog post and optional webhook. Configure per-team schedules, Confluence destinations, and an ART rollup from Admin Hub → "📋 Standup" tab.

- **Feature Change reports — ART Rollup (All Teams)**: A new "All Teams — ART Rollup" block in Admin Hub → Reports Config → Feature Change delivers a single combined Feature Change report covering every team in one Confluence page. Team labels are sourced automatically from the per-team configurations. The rollup runs on its own schedule and supports an optional Automation Trigger URL. A "Run Now" button is available for immediate manual delivery.
- **Admin Hub — ART View Settings — Jira Label field**: Each team row in ART View → Settings now has a "Jira Label" input. The label is stored on the team record and drives both the Feature Change report queries (Reports Hub) and the scheduled Feature Change delivery service. Labels are stored in `nodetoolbox-art-teams` localStorage alongside each team entry.
- **Feature Change report — label-based Jira query**: The Feature Change report now queries Jira using `type = Feature AND labels in ("TeamLabel")` instead of the previous Epic + project-key approach. In ART Combined mode a single unified query covers all configured team labels and results are grouped client-side by matching each issue's labels to its team. Individual team mode requires the team's Jira label to be configured in ART View → Settings.
- **Admin Hub — Reports Config tab**: A new top-level "Reports Config" tab replaces the Notifications section that previously lived inside the Config tab. Within Reports Config, two sub-tabs organise report delivery settings: "Scope Change" (the existing daily Scope Change reports with per-team and ART Rollup configuration) and "Feature Change" (new — see below).
- **Feature Change reports**: New daily report that monitors Feature-type issues for changes to Fix Version, Status, Target Start, Target End, and Due Date. Each ART team's Jira label (configured in ART Settings → Label Mapping) determines which Features are monitored. Each team has its own Confluence destination, schedule time, optional Target Blog URL, and Automation Trigger URL. Configured under Admin Hub → Reports Config → Feature Change.

### Fixed
- **Notifications — Automation Trigger webhook now authenticates correctly**: The webhook secret is now sent as the `X-Automation-Webhook-Token` HTTP request header, which is the authentication mechanism required by Confluence Cloud Automation incoming webhooks. Previous releases sent the secret as a query parameter, which Atlassian rejected with `{"errorMessages":["Missing token"],"status":400}`.

### Added
- **Notifications — Automation Trigger URL**: Each team notification config and the ART Rollup config now include an optional "Automation Trigger URL" field. After a report is successfully delivered to Confluence, NodeToolbox POSTs a JSON payload to that URL so a Confluence Automation rule (or any HTTP webhook consumer) can fire downstream notifications such as Teams messages or emails. The payload includes `teamName`, `projectKey`, `postUrl`, `generatedAt`, `releaseChangeCount`, and `sprintChangeCount`. Failures are logged but do not block delivery.

### Fixed
- **Notifications — Target Blog URL now appends instead of overwriting**: When a Target Blog URL is configured, each scheduled (or manual) delivery now prepends the new report above the existing page content, separated by a horizontal rule. The page accumulates a dated history of scope change reports rather than being replaced on every run.

### Added
- **Notifications — Multi-team Scope Change reports**: The Admin Hub Notifications section now supports one report configuration per ART team. Each team entry (auto-populated from ART View Settings) has its own Confluence Space Key, Target Blog URL, schedule time (HH:MM), and enable toggle. Reports are delivered independently on each team's configured schedule.
- **Notifications — ART Rollup report**: A new ART Rollup section in Admin Hub Notifications lets the RTE configure a single daily aggregate report covering all ART teams. The rollup includes a cross-team summary table followed by combined Release-change and Sprint-change tables (each with a Team column) in one Confluence page.
- **Reports Hub — Scope Change ART Combined mode**: The Scope Change tab now has a mode toggle. "Single Team" works as before. "ART Combined" runs parallel queries against every team configured in ART View Settings and displays all results in a unified Release-changes table and Sprint-changes table, each with a Team column for easy cross-team triage.
- **Reports Hub — Scope Change "Configure Scheduled Delivery" button**: A visible outlined button at the top-right of the Scope Change tab navigates directly to the Admin Hub Notifications section for configuring automated Confluence delivery.
- **Reports Hub — Scope Change controls merged into the global filter bar**: The Scope Change tab no longer has its own controls section. Team selection uses the existing "All Teams / specific team" filter; selecting "All Teams" runs ART Combined mode (all configured ART teams in parallel), selecting a specific team runs a single-team query. A time-window selector and Generate button appear in the filter bar alongside PI and Team when the Scope Change tab is active. The "⚙ Scheduled Delivery" shortcut button also sits in the filter bar for quick access to Admin Hub notification config.
- **Notifications — Target Blog URL**: A new optional "Target Blog URL" field in Admin Hub → Notifications. When set, NodeToolbox extracts the page ID from the URL and updates that existing Confluence page on every run instead of creating a new post. This keeps the URL stable so Confluence automation rules, bookmarks, and email forwards never break. Leave blank to keep the existing "create a new post each run" behaviour.

### Fixed
- **Notifications — Run Now no longer returns Confluence 401**: The scheduler was posting to `/rest/api/content` on the Atlassian Cloud root, which routes to Jira (not Confluence) and returns a Jira HTML login page as a 401 response. The correct Confluence REST API path on Atlassian Cloud includes the `/wiki` prefix — the request now goes to `/wiki/rest/api/content`, matching the path format used by the browser-side Confluence proxy.

### Added
- **Daily Scope Change delivery to Confluence**: A new server-side scheduler fires at 11:00 AM local time each day, queries Jira for fixVersion and sprint changes in the last 24 hours, and creates a Confluence blog post with the results. Empty days are skipped silently. The blog post appears in the space's built-in RSS/Atom feed, which can be wired to a Teams channel via the "Post RSS to channel" Workflow for automatic channel notifications.
- **Admin Hub — Notifications section**: New Config tab section to configure the daily delivery. Set the Confluence Space Key, Jira Project Key, and enable the schedule. A "Run Now" button triggers an immediate delivery cycle for testing without waiting for the scheduled time.

### Added
- **Reports Hub — Scope Change report**: New tab that surfaces issues that received a new Sprint or fixVersion value within a user-selected time window (7 / 14 / 30 / 60 days). Enter a project key, choose a window, and click Generate. Results are split into two sections — Release changes (fixVersion) and Sprint changes — each showing the issue, old value, new value, who made the change, and when. Uses the Jira changelog API (`expand=changelog`) so every re-plan is captured regardless of current field state. Useful for PI scope reviews, sprint retrospectives, and release integrity checks. Release and Sprint are fetched with separate queries because Jira does not support `sprint changed AFTER` as a history-search JQL predicate; sprint changes are discovered via `updated >= date` + client-side changelog filtering.

### Fixed
- **Feature Review — "Direct hygiene fixes" panel now shows which feature it applies to**: The panel header previously showed only the generic label "Direct hygiene fixes" with no feature context, making it look like a global bulk-action that would update all visible issues. The panel header now displays the feature issue key (e.g., `→ DENP-1286`) so it is clear the Fix Versions and Change Status actions apply only to that one feature.

### Fixed
- **Feature Review — "Missing Pointed Child Story" false positive with custom SP field**: The supplementary Jira query used JQL to re-discover which stories belong to which feature (via `cf[N] in (feature-keys) OR parent in (...)`). This is fragile because it depends on the Jira field being named "Feature Link" or "Epic Link" exactly, and on whether the `parent` field captures the Epic-Story link in this Jira configuration. The fix uses the blueprint hierarchy (which already knows the story→feature mapping) to build a direct `issueKey in (story-keys)` query instead — more reliable and independent of Jira field naming conventions.
- **Feature Review — "Missing Pointed Child Story" used wrong story-points source**: The Feature Review tab computes pointed-child status from `BlueprintStoryNode.storyPoints`, which the blueprint hierarchy hardcodes to `customfield_10016 / customfield_10028`. If a team's configured field is `customfield_10236` (Story Points Selection) and only that field is populated, `storyPoints` is always null and every feature flags as missing a pointed child. `fetchFeatureReviewItems` now accepts the configured field ID and runs a dedicated child-story Jira query that checks the correct field — consistent with the Hygiene and Pointing tabs.
- **Hygiene — "Missing Pointed Child Story" — feature link key not read from array-type fields**: Jira multi-value feature-link custom fields return an array of issue references (e.g. `[{key:"DENP-1286",…}]`). In JavaScript `typeof [] === 'object'`, so the array bypassed the array guard and fell into the object branch where `array.key` is `undefined`, causing `readLinkedFeatureKey` to return `null` for the child story instead of the parent feature key. The lookup then fell back to `issue.fields.parent.key`, which returned the story's own Jira epic (not the feature), so the feature was never added to the pointed-features set and was always falsely flagged. `readIssueKeyValue` now checks for arrays before the object branch and recurses into each element.
- **Hygiene — "Missing Pointed Child Story" child query now searches all feature-link fields**: The JQL that discovers child stories previously only queried the first feature-link field ID (`customfield_10108`). If the Jira instance stores the Feature Link in a different custom field (resolved by name at runtime), no children were found and every feature was falsely flagged. The query now ORs across every resolved feature-link field ID and also includes a `parent in (...)` clause so children linked via Jira's native parent-child hierarchy are found as well.
- **Hygiene — "Missing Pointed Child Story" now uses the configured story-points field**: The child-story lookup was hardcoded to `customfield_10028` and `customfield_10016`. It now fetches and checks the field configured in Settings (e.g. `customfield_10236`) as the authoritative source. The `hasPositiveStoryPoints` helper also now correctly handles Select-type `{id, value}` objects and numeric strings.

### Fixed
- **Hygiene — "None" treated as missing story points**: When a Jira Select-type story-points field has the placeholder option "None" explicitly selected, Jira returns `{id: "-1", value: "None"}`. The `hasEmptyStoryPoints` check previously recursed into the `value` string and returned `false` because `"None"` is not `null`. It now treats any string that does not parse as a positive finite number as empty — consistent with how the pointing queue's `parseNumericValue` has always handled it.

### Fixed
- **Hygiene tab (Sprint Dashboard) — automatically scoped to the active PI / sprint / fix version**: The Hygiene tab inside the Sprint Dashboard now pre-populates its extra JQL filter with the same scope as the rest of the dashboard (e.g. `AND cf[10301] = "25.1"` for PI mode).
